domain=.fidelity.com; path=/; secure\\n83: ****/\\n84: \\n85: \\n86: #include \\\"curl_setup.h\\\"\\n87: \\n88: #if !defined(CURL_DISABLE_HTTP) && !defined(CURL_DISABLE_COOKIES)\\n89: \\n90: #include \\\"urldata.h\\\"\\n91: #include \\\"cookie.h\\\"\\n92: #include \\\"psl.h\\\"\\n93: #include \\\"strtok.h\\\"\\n94: #include \\\"sendf.h\\\"\\n95: #include \\\"slist.h\\\"\\n96: #include \\\"share.h\\\"\\n97: #include \\\"strtoofft.h\\\"\\n98: #include \\\"strcase.h\\\"\\n99: #include \\\"curl_get_line.h\\\"\\n100: #include \\\"curl_memrchr.h\\\"\\n101: #include \\\"parsedate.h\\\"\\n102: #include \\\"rename.h\\\"\\n103: #include \\\"fopen.h\\\"\\n104: #include \\\"strdup.h\\\"\\n105: \\n106: /* The last 3 #include files should be in this order */\\n107: #include \\\"curl_printf.h\\\"\\n108: #include \\\"curl_memory.h\\\"\\n109: #include \\\"memdebug.h\\\"\\n110: \\n111: static void strstore(char **str, const char *newstr, size_t len);\\n112: \\n113: static void freecookie(struct Cookie *co)\\n114: {\\n115:   free(co->domain);\\n116:   free(co->path);\\n117:   free(co->spath);\\n118:   free(co->name);\\n119:   free(co->value);\\n120:   free(co);\\n121: }\\n122: \\n123: static bool cookie_tailmatch(const char *cookie_domain,\\n124:                              size_t cookie_domain_len,\\n125:                              const char *hostname)\\n126: {\\n127:   size_t hostname_len = strlen(hostname);\\n128: \\n129:   if(hostname_len < cookie_domain_len)\\n130:     return FALSE;\\n131: \\n132:   if(!strncasecompare(cookie_domain,\\n133:                       hostname + hostname_len-cookie_domain_len,\\n134:                       cookie_domain_len))\\n135:     return FALSE;\\n136: \\n137:   /*\\n138:    * A lead char of cookie_domain is not '.'.\\n139:    * RFC6265 4.1.2.3. The Domain Attribute says:\\n140:    * For example, if the value of the Domain attribute is\\n141:    * \\\"example.com\\\", the user agent will include the cookie in the Cookie\\n142:    * header when making HTTP requests to example.com, www.example.com, and\\n143:    * www.corp.example.com.\\n144:    */\\n145:   if(hostname_len == cookie_domain_len)\\n146:     return TRUE;\\n147:   if('.' == *(hostname + hostname_len - cookie_domain_len - 1))\\n148:     return TRUE;\\n149:   return FALSE;\\n150: }\\n151: \\n152: /*\\n153:  * matching cookie path and url path\\n154:  * RFC6265 5.1.4 Paths and Path-Match\\n155:  */\\n156: static bool pathmatch(const char *cookie_path, const char *request_uri)\\n157: {\\n158:   size_t cookie_path_len;\\n159:   size_t uri_path_len;\\n160:   char *uri_path = NULL;\\n161:   char *pos;\\n162:   bool ret = FALSE;\\n163: \\n164:   /* cookie_path must not have last '/' separator. ex: /sample */\\n165:   cookie_path_len = strlen(cookie_path);\\n166:   if(1 == cookie_path_len) {\\n167:     /* cookie_path must be '/' */\\n168:     return TRUE;\\n169:   }\\n170: \\n171:   uri_path = strdup(request_uri);\\n172:   if(!uri_path)\\n173:     return FALSE;\\n174:   pos = strchr(uri_path, '?');\\n175:   if(pos)\\n176:     *pos = 0x0;\\n177: \\n178:   /* #-fragments are already cut off! */\\n179:   if(0 == strlen(uri_path) || uri_path[0] != '/') {\\n180:     strstore(&uri_path, \\\"/\\\", 1);\\n181:     if(!uri_path)\\n182:       return FALSE;\\n183:   }\\n184: \\n185:   /*\\n186:    * here, RFC6265 5.1.4 says\\n187:    *  4. Output the characters of the uri-path from the first character up\\n188:    *     to, but not including, the right-most %x2F (\\\"/\\\").\\n189:    *  but URL path /hoge?fuga=xxx means /hoge/index.cgi?fuga=xxx in some site\\n190:    *  without redirect.\\n191:    *  Ignore this algorithm because /hoge is uri path for this case\\n192:    *  (uri path is not /).\\n193:    */\\n194: \\n195:   uri_path_len = strlen(uri_path);\\n196: \\n197:   if(uri_path_len < cookie_path_len) {\\n198:     ret = FALSE;\\n199:     goto pathmatched;\\n200:   }\\n201: \\n202:   /* not using checkprefix() because matching should be case-sensitive */\\n203:   if(strncmp(cookie_path, uri_path, cookie_path_len)) {\\n204:     ret = FALSE;\\n205:     goto pathmatched;\\n206:   }\\n207: \\n208:   /* The cookie-path and the uri-path are identical. */\\n209:   if(cookie_path_len == uri_path_len) {\\n210:     ret = TRUE;\\n211:     goto pathmatched;\\n212:   }\\n213: \\n214:   /* here, cookie_path_len < uri_path_len */\\n215:   if(uri_path[cookie_path_len] == '/') {\\n216:     ret = TRUE;\\n217:     goto pathmatched;\\n218:   }\\n219: \\n220:   ret = FALSE;\\n221: \\n222: pathmatched:\\n223:   free(uri_path);\\n224:   return ret;\\n225: }\\n226: \\n227: /*\\n228:  * Return the top-level domain, for optimal hashing.\\n229:  */\\n230: static const char *get_top_domain(const char * const domain, size_t *outlen)\\n231: {\\n232:   size_t len = 0;\\n233:   const char *first = NULL, *last;\\n234: \\n235:   if(domain) {\\n236:     len = strlen(domain);\\n237:     last = memrchr(domain, '.', len);\\n238:     if(last) {\\n239:       first = memrchr(domain, '.', (last - domain));\\n240:       if(first)\\n241:         len -= (++first - domain);\\n242:     }\\n243:   }\\n244: \\n245:   if(outlen)\\n246:     *outlen = len;\\n247: \\n248:   return first? first: domain;\\n249: }\\n250: \\n251: /* Avoid C1001, an \\\"internal error\\\" with MSVC14 */\\n252: #if defined(_MSC_VER) && (_MSC_VER == 1900)\\n253: #pragma optimize(\\\"\\\", off)\\n254: #endif\\n255: \\n256: /*\\n257:  * A case-insensitive hash for the cookie domains.\\n258:  */\\n259: static size_t cookie_hash_domain(const char *domain, const size_t len)\\n260: {\\n261:   const char *end = domain + len;\\n262:   size_t h = 5381;\\n263: \\n264:   while(domain < end) {\\n265:     h += h << 5;\\n266:     h ^= Curl_raw_toupper(*domain++);\\n267:   }\\n268: \\n269:   return (h % COOKIE_HASH_SIZE);\\n270: }\\n271: \\n272: #if defined(_MSC_VER) && (_MSC_VER == 1900)\\n273: #pragma optimize(\\\"\\\", on)\\n274: #endif\\n275: \\n276: /*\\n277:  * Hash this domain.\\n278:  */\\n279: static size_t cookiehash(const char * const domain)\\n280: {\\n281:   const char *top;\\n282:   size_t len;\\n283: \\n284:   if(!domain || Curl_host_is_ipnum(domain))\\n285:     return 0;\\n286: \\n287:   top = get_top_domain(domain, &len);\\n288:   return cookie_hash_domain(top, len);\\n289: }\\n290: \\n291: /*\\n292:  * cookie path sanitize\\n293:  */\\n294: static char *sanitize_cookie_path(const char *cookie_path)\\n295: {\\n296:   size_t len;\\n297:   char *new_path = strdup(cookie_path);\\n298:   if(!new_path)\\n299:     return NULL;\\n300: \\n301:   /* some stupid site sends path attribute with '\\\"'. */\\n302:   len = strlen(new_path);\\n303:   if(new_path[0] == '\\\\\\\"') {\\n304:     memmove(new_path, new_path + 1, len);\\n305:     len--;\\n306:   }\\n307:   if(len && (new_path[len - 1] == '\\\\\\\"')) {\\n308:     new_path[--len] = 0x0;\\n309:   }\\n310: \\n311:   /* RFC6265 5.2.4 The Path Attribute */\\n312:   if(new_path[0] != '/') {\\n313:     /* Let cookie-path be the default-path. */\\n314:     strstore(&new_path, \\\"/\\\", 1);\\n315:     return new_path;\\n316:   }\\n317: \\n318:   /* convert /hoge/ to /hoge */\\n319:   if(len && new_path[len - The caller is responsible for checking\\n361:  * for OOM errors.\\n362:  */\\n363: static void strstore(char **str, const char *newstr, size_t len)\\n364: {\\n365:   DEBUGASSERT(newstr);\\n366:   DEBUGASSERT(str);\\n367:   free(*str);\\n368:   *str = Curl_memdup(newstr, len + 1);\\n369:   if(*str)\\n370:     (*str)[len] = 0;\\n371: }\\n372: \\n373: /*\\n374:  * remove_expired\\n375:  *\\n376:  * Remove expired cookies from the hash by inspecting the expires timestamp on\\n377:  * each cookie in the hash, freeing and deleting any where the timestamp is in\\n378:  * the past.  If the cookiejar has recorded the next timestamp at which one or\\n379:  * more cookies expire, then processing will exit early in case this timestamp\\n380:  * is in the future.\\n381:  */\\n382: static void remove_expired(struct CookieInfo *cookies)\\n383: {\\n384:   struct Cookie *co, *nx;\\n385:   curl_off_t now = (curl_off_t)time(NULL);\\n386:   unsigned int i;\\n387: \\n388:   /*\\n389:    * If the earliest expiration timestamp in the jar is in the future we can\\n390:    * skip scanning the whole jar and instead exit early as there won't be any\\n391:    * cookies to evict.  If we need to evict however, reset the next_expiration\\n392:    * counter in order to track the next one. In case the recorded first\\n393:    * expiration is the max offset, then perform the safe fallback of checking\\n394:    * all cookies.\\n395:    */\\n396:   if(now < cookies->next_expiration &&\\n397:       cookies->next_expiration != CURL_OFF_T_MAX)\\n398:     return;\\n399:   else\\n400:     cookies->next_expiration = CURL_OFF_T_MAX;\\n401: \\n402:   for(i = 0; i < COOKIE_HASH_SIZE; i++) {\\n403:     struct Cookie *pv = NULL;\\n404:     co = cookies->cookies[i];\\n405:     while(co) {\\n406:       nx = co->next;\\n407:       if(co->expires && co->expires < now) {\\n408:         if(!pv) {\\n409:           cookies->cookies[i] = co->next;\\n410:         }\\n411:         else {\\n412:           pv->next = co->next;\\n413:         }\\n414:         cookies->numcookies--;\\n415:         freecookie(co);\\n416:       }\\n417:       else {\\n418:         /*\\n419:          * If this cookie has an expiration timestamp earlier than what we've\\n420:          * seen so far then record it for the next round of expirations.\\n421:          */\\n422:         if(co->expires && co->expires < cookies->next_expiration)\\n423:           cookies->next_expiration = co->expires;\\n424:         pv = co;\\n425:       }\\n426:       co = nx;\\n427:     }\\n428:   }\\n429: }\\n430: \\n431: /* Make sure domain contains a dot or is localhost. */\\n432: static bool bad_domain(const char *domain, size_t len)\\n433: {\\n434:   if((len == 9) && strncasecompare(domain, \\\"localhost\\\", 9))\\n435:     return FALSE;\\n436:   else {\\n437:     /* there must be a dot present, but that dot must not be a trailing dot */\\n438:     char *dot = memchr(domain, '.', len);\\n439:     if(dot) {\\n440:       size_t i = dot - domain;\\n441:       if((len - i) > 1)\\n442:         /* the dot is not the last byte */\\n443:         return FALSE;\\n444:     }\\n445:   }\\n446:   return TRUE;\\n447: }\\n448: \\n449: /*\\n450:   RFC 6265 section 4.1.1 says a server should accept this range:\\n451: \\n452:   cookie-octet    = %x21 / %x23-2B / %x2D-3A / %x3C-5B / %x5D-7E\\n453: \\n454:   But Firefox and Chrome as of June 2022 accept space, comma and double-quotes\\n455:   fine. The prime reason for filtering out control bytes is that some HTTP\\n456:   servers return 400 for requests that contain such.\\n457: */\\n458: static int invalid_octets(const char *p)\\n459: {\\n460:   /* Reject all bytes \\\\x01 - \\\\x1f (*except* \\\\x09, TAB) + \\\\x7f */\\n461:   static const char badoctets[] = {\\n462:     \\\"\\\\x01\\\\x02\\\\x03\\\\x04\\\\x05\\\\x06\\\\x07\\\\x08\\\\x0a\\\"\\n463:     \\\"\\\\x0b\\\\x0c\\\\x0d\\\\x0e\\\\x0f\\\\x10\\\\x11\\\\x12\\\\x13\\\\x14\\\"\\n464:     \\\"\\\\x15\\\\x16\\\\x17\\\\x18\\\\x19\\\\x1a\\\\x1b\\\\x1c\\\\x1d\\\\x1e\\\\x1f\\\\x7f\\\"\\n465:   };\\n466:   size_t len;\\n467:   /* scan for all the octets that are *not* in cookie-octet */\\n468:   len = strcspn(p, badoctets);\\n469:   return (p[len] != '\\\\0');\\n470: }\\n471: \\n472: /*\\n473:  * Curl_cookie_add\\n474:  *\\n475:  * Add a single cookie line to the cookie keeping object. Be aware that\\n476:  * sometimes we get an IP-only host name, and that might also be a numerical\\n477:  * IPv6 address.\\n478:  *\\n479:  * Returns NULL on out of memory or invalid cookie. This is suboptimal,\\n480:  * as they should be treated separately.\\n481:  */\\n482: struct Cookie *\\n483: Curl_cookie_add(struct Curl_easy *data,\\n484:                 struct CookieInfo *c,\\n485:                 bool httpheader, /* TRUE if HTTP header-style line */\\n486:                 bool noexpire, /* if TRUE, skip remove_expired() */\\n487:                 const char *lineptr,   /* first character of the line */\\n488:                 const char *domain, /* default domain */\\n489:                 const char *path,   /* full path used when this cookie is set,\\n490: */\\n493: {\\n494:   struct Cookie *clist;\\n495:   struct Cookie *co;\\n496:   struct Cookie *lastc = NULL;\\n497:   struct Cookie *replace_co = NULL;\\n498:   struct Cookie *replace_clist = NULL;\\n499:   time_t now = time(NULL);\\n500:   bool replace_old = FALSE;\\n501:   bool badcookie = FALSE; /* cookies are good by default. mmmmm yummy */\\n502:   size_t myhash;\\n503: \\n504:   DEBUGASSERT(data);\\n505:   DEBUGASSERT(MAX_SET_COOKIE_AMOUNT <= 255); /* counter is an unsigned char */\\n506:   if(data->req.setcookies >= MAX_SET_COOKIE_AMOUNT)\\n507:     return NULL;\\n508: \\n509:   /* First, alloc and init a new struct for it */\\n510:   co = calloc(1, sizeof(struct Cookie));\\n511:   if(!co)\\n512:     return NULL; /* bail out if we're this low on memory */\\n513: \\n514:   if(httpheader) {\\n515:     /* This line was read off an HTTP-header */\\n516:     const char *ptr;\\n517: \\n518:     size_t linelength = strlen(lineptr);\\n519:     if(linelength > MAX_COOKIE_LINE) {\\n520:       /* discard overly long lines at once */\\n521:       free(co);\\n522:       return NULL;\\n523:     }\\n524: \\n525:     ptr = lineptr;\\n526:     do {\\n527:       size_t vlen;\\n528:       size_t nlen;\\n529: \\n530:       while(*ptr && ISBLANK(*ptr))\\n531:         ptr++;\\n532: \\n533:       /* we have a <name>=<value> pair or a stand-alone word here */\\n534:       nlen = strcspn(ptr, \\\";\\\\t\\\\r\\\\n=\\\");\\n535:       if(nlen) {\\n536:         bool done = FALSE;\\n537:         bool sep = FALSE;\\n538:         const char *namep = 1]))\\n545:           nlen--;\\n546: \\n547:         if(*ptr == '=') {\\n548:           vlen = strcspn(++ptr, \\\";\\\\r\\\\n\\\");\\n549:           valuep = ptr;\\n550:           sep = TRUE;\\n551: \\n557:           /* Skip leading whitespace from the value */\\n558:           while(vlen && ISBLANK(*valuep)) {\\n559:             valuep++;\\n560:             vlen--;\\n561:           }\\n562: \\n563:           /* Reject cookies with a TAB inside the value */\\n564:           if(memchr(valuep, '\\\\t', vlen)) {\\n565:             freecookie(co);\\n566:             infof(data, \\\"cookie }\\n574: \\n575:         /*\\n576:          * Check for too long individual name or contents, or too long\\n577:          * combination of name + contents. * headers that have the same string property set more than once,\\n604:          * and then we use the last one.\\n605:          */\\n606: \\n607:         if(!co->name) {\\n608:           /* The very first name/value pair is the actual cookie name */\\n609:           if(!sep) {\\n610:             /* Bad name/value pair. */\\n611:             badcookie = TRUE;\\n612:             break;\\n613:           }\\n614:           strstore(&co->name, namep, nlen);\\n615:           strstore(&co->value, valuep, vlen);\\n616:           done = TRUE;\\n617:           if(!co->name || !co->value) {\\n618:             badcookie = TRUE;\\n619:             break;\\n620:           }\\n621:           if(invalid_octets(co->value) || invalid_octets(co->name)) {\\n622:             infof(data, \\\"invalid octets in /*\\n634:            * secure cookies are only allowed to be set when the connection is\\n635:            * using a secure protocol, or when the cookie is being set by\\n636:            * reading from free(co->spath); /* if this is set again */\\n662:           co->spath = sanitize_cookie_path(co->path);\\n663:           if(!co->spath) {\\n664:             badcookie = TRUE; /* out of memory bad */\\n665:             break;\\n666:           }\\n667:         }\\n668:         else if((nlen == 6) &&\\n669:                 strncasecompare(\\\"domain\\\", namep, 6) && vlen) {\\n670:           bool is_ip;\\n671: \\n672:           /*\\n673:            * Now, we make sure that our host is within the given domain, or\\n674:            * the given domain is not valid and thus cannot be set.\\n675:            */\\n676: \\n677:           if('.' == valuep[0]) {\\n678:             valuep++; /* ignore preceding dot */\\n679:             vlen--;\\n680:           }\\n681: \\n682: #ifndef USE_LIBPSL\\n683:           /*\\n684:            * Without PSL we don't know when the incoming cookie is set on a\\n685:            * TLD or otherwise \\\"protected\\\" suffix. The creationtime is guaranteed to\\n1293:  * be unique per cookie, so we know we will get an ordering at that point.\\n1294:  */\\n1295: static int cookie_sort(const void *p1, const void *p2)\\n1296: {\\n1297:   struct Cookie *c1 = *(struct Cookie **)p1;\\n1298:   struct Cookie *c2 = *(struct Cookie **)p2;\\n1299:   size_t l1, l2;\\n1300: \\n1301:   /* 1 - compare cookie path lengths */\\n1302:   l1 = c1->path ? If the cookiejar has recorded the next timestamp at which one or\n379:  * more cookies expire, then processing will exit early in case this timestamp\n380:  * is in the future.\n381:  */\n382: static void remove_expired(struct CookieInfo *cookies)\n383: {\n384:   struct Cookie *co, *nx;\n385:   curl_off_t now = (curl_off_t)time(NULL);\n386:   unsigned int i;\n387: \n388:   /*\n389:    * If the earliest expiration timestamp in the jar is in the future we can\n390:    * skip scanning the whole jar and instead exit early as there won't be any\n391:    * cookies to evict.  If we need to evict however, reset the next_expiration\n392:    * counter in order to track the next one. Pass in the 'newurl' string\n1497:  * as given by the remote server and set up the new URL to request.\n1498:  *\n1499:  * This function DOES NOT FREE the given url.\n1500:  */\n1501: CURLcode Curl_follow(struct Curl_easy *data,\n1502:                      char *newurl,    /* the Location: string */\n1503:                      followtype type) /* see transfer.h */\n1504: {\n1505: #ifdef CURL_DISABLE_HTTP\n1506:   (void)data;\n1507:   (void)newurl;\n1508:   (void)type;\n1509:   /* Location: following will not happen when HTTP is disabled */\n1510:   return CURLE_TOO_MANY_REDIRECTS;\n1511: #else\n1512: \n1513:   /* Location: redirect */\n1514:   bool disallowport = FALSE;\n1515:   bool reachedmax = FALSE;\n1516:   CURLUcode uc;\n1517: \n1518:   DEBUGASSERT(type != FOLLOW_NONE);\n1519: \n1520:   if(type != FOLLOW_FAKE)\n1521:     data->state.requests++; /* count all real follows */\n1522:   if(type == FOLLOW_REDIR) {\n1523:     if((data->set.maxredirs != -1) &&\n1524:        (data->state.followlocation >= data->set.maxredirs)) {\n1525:       reachedmax = TRUE;\n1526:       type = FOLLOW_FAKE; /* switch to fake to store the would-be-redirected\n1527:                              to URL */\n1528:     }\n1529:     else {\n1530:       data->state.followlocation++; /* count redirect-followings, including\n1531:                                        auth reloads */\n1532: \n1533:       if(data->set.http_auto_referer) {\n1534:         CURLU *u;\n1535:         char *referer = NULL;\n1536: \n1537:         /* We are asked to automatically set the previous URL as the referer\n1538:            when we get the next URL. We pick the ->url field, which may or may\n1539:            not be 100% correct */\n1540: \n1541:         if(data->state.referer_alloc) {\n1542:           Curl_safefree(data->state.referer);\n1543:           data->state.referer_alloc = FALSE;\n1544:         }\n1545: \n1546:         /* Make a copy of the URL without credentials and fragment */\n1547:         u = curl_url();\n1548:         if(!u)\n1549:           return CURLE_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n1550: \n1551:         uc = curl_url_set(u, CURLUPART_URL, data->state.url, 0);\n1552:         if(!uc)\n1553:           uc = curl_url_set(u, CURLUPART_FRAGMENT, NULL, 0);\n1554:         if(!uc)\n1555:           uc = curl_url_set(u, CURLUPART_USER, NULL, 0);\n1556:         if(!uc)\n1557:           uc = curl_url_set(u, CURLUPART_PASSWORD, NULL, 0);\n1558:         if(!uc)\n1559:           uc = curl_url_get(u, CURLUPART_URL, &referer, 0);\n1560: \n1561:         curl_url_cleanup(u);\n1562: \n1563:         if(uc || !referer)\n1564:           return CURLE_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n1565: \n1566:         data->state.referer = referer;\n1567:         data->state.referer_alloc = TRUE; /* yes, free this later */\n1568:       }\n1569:     }\n1570:   }\n1571: \n1572:   if((type != FOLLOW_RETRY) &&\n1573:      (data->req.httpcode != 401) && (data->req.httpcode != 407) &&\n1574:      Curl_is_absolute_url(newurl, NULL, 0, FALSE)) {\n1575:     /* If this is not redirect due to a 401 or 407 response and an absolute\n1576:        URL: don't allow a custom port number */\n1577:     disallowport = TRUE;\n1578:   }\n1579: \n1580:   DEBUGASSERT(data->state.uh);\n1581:   uc = curl_url_set(data->state.uh, CURLUPART_URL, newurl,\n1582:                     (type == FOLLOW_FAKE) ? unless permitted */\n1606:     if(!data->set.allow_auth_to_other_hosts && (type != FOLLOW_FAKE)) {\n1607:       char *portnum;\n1608:       int port;\n1609:       bool clear = FALSE;\n1610: \n1611:           return Curl_uc_to_curlcode(uc);\n1636:         }\n1637: \n1638:         p = Curl_builtin_scheme(scheme, CURL_ZERO_TERMINATED);\n1639:         if(p && (p->protocol !=        }\n1644:         free(scheme);\n1645:       }\n1646:       if(clear) {\n1647:         Curl_safefree(data->state.aptr.user);\n1648:         Curl_safefree(data->state.aptr.passwd);\n1649:       }\n1650:     }\n1651:   }\n1652: \n1653:   if(type == FOLLOW_FAKE) {\n1654:     /* we're only figuring out the new url if we would've followed locations\n1655:        but now we're done so we can get out! */\n1656:     data->info.wouldredirect = newurl;\n1657: \n1658:     if(reachedmax) {\n1659:       failf(data, \"Maximum (%ld) redirects followed\", data->set.maxredirs);\n1660:       return We need to perform\n1678:    * differently based on exactly what return code there was.\n1679:    *\n1680:    * News from 7.10.6: we can also get here on a 401 or 407, in case we act on\n1681:    * an HTTP (proxy-) authentication scheme other than Basic.\n1682:    */\n1683:   switch(data->info.httpcode) {\n1684:     /* 401 - Act on a WWW-Authenticate, we keep on moving and do the\n1685:        Authorization: XXXX header in the HTTP request code snippet */\n1686:     /* 407 - Act on a Proxy-Authenticate, we keep on moving and do the\n1687:        Proxy-Authorization: XXXX header in the HTTP request code snippet */\n1688:     /* 300 - Multiple Choices */\n1689:     /* 306 - Not used */\n1690:     /* 307 - Temporary Redirect */\n1691:   default:  /* for all above (and the unknown ones) */\n1692:     /* Some codes are explicitly mentioned since I've checked RFC2616 and they\n1693:      * seem to be OK to POST to.\n1694:      */\n1695:     break;\n1696:   case 301: /* Moved Permanently */\n1697:     /* (quote from RFC7231, section 6.4.2)\n1698:      *\n1699:      * Note: For historical reasons, a user agent MAY change the request\n1700:      * method from POST to GET for the subsequent request.  If this\n1701:      * behavior is undesired, the 307 (Temporary Redirect) status code\n1702:      * can be used instead.\n1703:      *\n1704:      * ----\n1705:      *\n1706:      * Many webservers expect this, so these servers often answers to a POST\n1707:      * request with an error page. To be sure that libcurl gets the page that\n1708:      * most user agents would get, libcurl has to force GET.\n1709:      *\n1710:      * This behavior is forbidden by RFC1945 and the obsolete RFC2616, and\n1711:      * can be overridden with CURLOPT_POSTREDIR.\n1712:      */\n1713:     if((data->state.httpreq == HTTPREQ_POST\n1714:         || data->state.httpreq == HTTPREQ_POST_FORM\n1715:         || data->state.httpreq == HTTPREQ_POST_MIME)\n1716:        && !(data->set.keep_post & CURL_REDIR_POST_301)) {\n1717:       infof(data, \"Switch from POST to GET\");\n1718:       data->state.httpreq = HTTPREQ_GET;\n1719:     }\n1720:     break;\n1721:   case 302: /* Found */\n1722:     /* (quote from RFC7231, section 6.4.3)\n1723:      *\n1724:      * Note: For historical reasons, a user agent MAY change the request\n1725:      * method from POST to GET for the subsequent request.  If this\n1726:      * behavior is undesired, the 307 (Temporary Redirect) status code\n1727:      * can be used instead.\n1728:      *\n1729:      * ----\n1730:      *\n1731:      * Many webservers expect this, so these servers often answers to a POST\n1732:      * request with an error page. To be sure that libcurl gets the page that\n1733:      * most user agents would get, libcurl has to force GET.\n1734:      *\n1735:      * This behavior is forbidden by RFC1945 and the obsolete RFC2616, and\n1736:      * can be overridden with CURLOPT_POSTREDIR.\n1737:      */\n1738:     if((data->state.httpreq == HTTPREQ_POST\n1739:         || data->state.httpreq == HTTPREQ_POST_FORM\n1740:         || data->state.httpreq == HTTPREQ_POST_MIME)\n1741:        && !(data->set.keep_post & CURL_REDIR_POST_302)) {\n1742:       infof(data, \"Switch from POST to GET\");\n1743:       data->state.httpreq = HTTPREQ_GET;\n1744:     }\n1745:     break;\n1746: \n1747:   case 303: /* See Other */\n1748:     /* 'See Other' location is not the resource but a substitute for the\n1749:      * resource. In this case we switch the method to GET/HEAD, unless the\n1750:      * method is POST and the user specified to keep it as POST.\n1751:      * https://github.com/curl/curl/issues/5237#issuecomment-614641049\n1752:      */\n1753:     if(data->state.httpreq != HTTPREQ_GET &&\n1754:        ((data->state.httpreq != HTTPREQ_POST &&\n1755:          data->state.httpreq != HTTPREQ_POST_FORM &&\n1756:          data->state.httpreq != HTTPREQ_POST_MIME) ||\n1757:         !(data->set.keep_post & CURL_REDIR_POST_303))) {\n1758:       data->state.httpreq = HTTPREQ_GET;\n1759:       infof(data, \"Switch to %s\",\n1760:             data->req.no_body?\"HEAD\":\"GET\");\n1761:     }\n1762:     break;\n1763:   case 304: /* Not Modified */\n1764:     /* 304 means we did a conditional request and it was \"Not modified\".\n1765:      * We shouldn't get any Location: header in this response!\n1766:      */\n1767:     break;\n1768:   case 305: /* Use Proxy */\n1769:     /* (quote from RFC2616, section 10.3.6):\n1770:      * \"The requested resource MUST be accessed through the proxy given\n1771:      * by the Location field. The Location field gives the URI of the\n1772:      * proxy.  The recipient is expected to repeat this single request\n1773:      * via the proxy. 305 responses MUST only be generated by origin\n1774:      * servers.\"\n1775:      */\n1776:     break;\n1777:   }\n1778:   Curl_pgrsTime(data, TIMER_REDIRECT);\n1779:   Curl_pgrsResetTransferSizes(data);\n1780: \n1781:   return CURLE_OK;\n1782: #endif /* CURL_DISABLE_HTTP */\n1783: }\n1784: \n1785: /* Returns CURLE_OK *and* sets '*url' if a request retry is wanted.\n1786: \n1787:    NOTE: that the *url is malloc()ed. */\n1788: CURLcode Curl_retry_request(struct Curl_easy *data, char **url)\n1789: {\n1790:   struct connectdata *conn = data->conn;\n1791:   bool retry = FALSE;\n1792:   *url = NULL;\n1793: \n1794:   /* if we're talking upload, we can't do the checks below, unless the protocol\n1795:      is HTTP as when uploading over HTTP we will still get a response */\n1796:   if(data->state.upload &&\n1797:      !(conn->handler->protocol&(PROTO_FAMILY_HTTP|CURLPROTO_RTSP)))\n1798:     return CURLE_OK;\n1799: \n1800:   if((data->req.bytecount + data->req.headerbytecount == 0) &&\n1801:      conn->bits.reuse &&\n1802:      (!data->req.no_body || (conn->handler->protocol & PROTO_FAMILY_HTTP))\n1803: #ifndef CURL_DISABLE_RTSP\n1804:      && (data->set.rtspreq != RTSPREQ_RECEIVE)\n1805: #endif\n1806:     )\n1807:     /* We got no data, we attempted to reuse a connection. For HTTP this\n1808:        can be a retry so we try again regardless if we expected a body.\n1809:        For other protocols we only try again only if we expected a body.\n1810: \n1811:        This might happen if the connection was left alive when we were\n1812:        done using it before, but that was closed when we wanted to read from\n1813:        it again. Bad luck. Retry the same request on a fresh connect! */\n1814:     retry = TRUE;\n1815:   else if(data->state.refused_stream &&\n1816:           (data->req.bytecount + data->req.headerbytecount == 0) ) {\n1817:     /* This was sent on a refused stream, safe to rerun. A refused stream\n1818:        error can typically only happen on HTTP/2 level if the stream is safe\n1819:        to issue again, but the nghttp2 API can deliver the message to other\n1820:        streams as well, which is why this adds the check the data counters\n1821:        too. */\n1822:     infof(data, \"REFUSED_STREAM, retrying a fresh connect\");\n1823:     data->state.refused_stream = FALSE; /* clear again */\n1824:     retry = TRUE;\n1825:   }\n1826:   if(retry) {\n1827: #define CONN_MAX_RETRIES 5\n1828:     if(data->state.retrycount++ >= CONN_MAX_RETRIES) {\n1829:       failf(data, \"Connection died, tried %d times before giving up\",\n1830:             CONN_MAX_RETRIES);\n1831:       data->state.retrycount = 0;\n1832:       return CURLE_SEND_ERROR;\n1833:     }\n1834:     infof(data, \"Connection died, retrying a fresh connect (retry count: %d)\",\n1835:           data->state.retrycount);\n1836:     *url = strdup(data->state.url);\n1837:     if(!*url)\n1838:       return CURLE_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n1839: \n1840:     connclose(conn, \"retry\"); /* close this connection */\n1841:     conn->bits.retry = TRUE; /* mark this as a connection we're about\n1842:                                 to retry. Marking it this way should\n1843:                                 prevent i.e HTTP transfers to return\n1844:                                 error just because nothing has been\n1845:                                 transferred! */\n1846: \n1847: \n1848:     if((conn->handler->protocol&PROTO_FAMILY_HTTP) &&\n1849:        data->req.writebytecount) {\n1850:       data->state.rewindbeforesend = TRUE;\n1851:       infof(data, \"state.rewindbeforesend = TRUE\");\n1852:     }\n1853:   }\n1854:   return CURLE_OK;\n1855: }\n1856: \n1857: /*\n1858:  * Curl_setup_transfer() is called to setup some basic properties for the\n1859:  * upcoming transfer.\n1860:  */\n1861: void\n1862: Curl_setup_transfer(\n1863:   struct Curl_easy *data,   /* transfer */\n1864:   int sockindex,            /* socket index to read from or -1 */\n1865:   curl_off_t size,          /* -1 if unknown at this point */\n1866:   bool getheader,           /* TRUE if header parsing is wanted */\n1867:   int writesockindex        /* socket index to write to, it may very well be\n1868:                                the same we read from. -1 disables */\n1869:   )\n1870: {\n1871:   struct SingleRequest *k = &data->req;\n1872:   struct connectdata *conn = data->conn;\n1873:   struct HTTP *http = data->req.p.http;\n1874:   bool httpsending;\n1875: \n1876:   DEBUGASSERT(conn != NULL);\n1877:   DEBUGASSERT((sockindex <= 1) && (sockindex >= -1));\n1878: \n1879:   httpsending = ((conn->handler->protocol&PROTO_FAMILY_HTTP) &&\n1880:                  (http->sending == HTTPSEND_REQUEST));\n1881: \n1882:   if(conn->bits.multiplex || conn->httpversion >= 20 || httpsending) {\n1883:     /* when multiplexing, the read/write sockets need to be the same! */\n1884:     conn->sockfd = sockindex == -1 ?\n1885:       ((writesockindex == -1 ? CURL_SOCKET_BAD : conn->sock[writesockindex])) :\n1886:       conn->sock[sockindex];\n1887:     conn->writesockfd = conn->sockfd;\n1888:     if(httpsending)\n1889:       /* special and very HTTP-specific */\n1890:       writesockindex = FIRSTSOCKET;\n1891:   }\n1892:   else {\n1893:     conn->sockfd = sockindex == -1 ?\n1894:       CURL_SOCKET_BAD : conn->sock[sockindex];\n1895:     conn->writesockfd = writesockindex == -1 ?\n1896:       CURL_SOCKET_BAD:conn->sock[writesockindex];\n1897:   }\n1898:   k->getheader = getheader;\n1899: \n1900:   k->size = size;\n1901: \n1902:   /* The code sequence below is placed in this function just because all\n1903:      necessary input is not always known in do_complete() as this function may\n1904:      be called after that */\n1905: \n1906:   if(!k->getheader) {\n1907:     k->header = FALSE;\n1908:     if(size > 0)\n1909:       Curl_pgrsSetDownloadSize(data, size);\n1910:   }\n1911:   /* we want header and/or body, if neither then don't do this! */\n1912:   if(k->getheader || !data->req.no_body) {\n1913: \n1914:     if(sockindex != -1)\n1915:       k->keepon |= KEEP_RECV;\n1916: \n1917:     if(writesockindex != -1) {\n1918:       /* HTTP 1.1 magic:\n1919: \n1920:          Even if we require a 100-return code before uploading data, we might\n1921:          need to write data before that since the REQUEST may not have been\n1922:          finished sent off just yet.\n1923: \n1924:          Thus, we must check if the request has been sent before we set the\n1925:          state info where we wait for the 100-return code\n1926:       */\n1927:       if((data->state.expect100header) &&\n1928:          (conn->handler->protocol&PROTO_FAMILY_HTTP) &&\n1929:          (http->sending == HTTPSEND_BODY)) {\n1930:         /* wait with write until we either got 100-continue or a timeout */\n1931:         k->exp100 = EXP100_AWAITING_CONTINUE;\n1932:         k->start100 = Curl_now();\n1933: \n1934:         /* Set a timeout for the multi interface. Add the inaccuracy margin so\n1935:            that we don't fire slightly too early and get denied to run. */\n1936:         Curl_expire(data, data->set.expect_100_timeout, EXPIRE_100_TIMEOUT);\n1937:       }\n1938:       else {\n1939:         if(data->state.expect100header)\n1940:           /* when we've sent off the rest of the headers, we must await a\n1941:              100-continue but first finish sending the request */\n1942:           k->exp100 = EXP100_SENDING_REQUEST;\n1943: \n1944:         /* enable the write bit when we're not waiting for continue */\n1945:         k->keepon |= KEEP_SEND;\n1946:       }\n1947:     } /* if(writesockindex != -1) */\n1948:   } /* if(k->getheader || !data->req.no_body) */\n1949: \n1950: }\n1951: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/curl--09e25b9d@38a2cef1e44568cc397af3ee85e19532e8f889a5/-/blob/lib/transfer.c"}}}

The Domain Attribute says:\\n140:    * For example, if the value of the Domain attribute is\\n141:    * \\\"example.com\\\", the user agent will include the cookie in the Cookie\\n142:    * header when making HTTP requests to example.com, www.example.com, and\\n143:    * www.corp.example.com.\\n144:    */\\n145:   if(hostname_len == cookie_domain_len)\\n146:     return TRUE;\\n147:   if('.' == *(hostname + hostname_len - cookie_domain_len - 1))\\n148:     return TRUE;\\n149:   return FALSE;\\n150: }\\n151: \\n152: /*\\n153:  * matching cookie path and url path\\n154:  * RFC6265 5.1.4 Paths and Path-Match\\n155:  */\\n156: static bool pathmatch(const char *cookie_path, const char *request_uri)\\n157: {\\n158:   size_t cookie_path_len;\\n159:   size_t uri_path_len;\\n160:   char *uri_path = NULL;\\n161:   char *pos;\\n162:   bool ret = FALSE;\\n163: \\n164:   /* cookie_path must not have last '/' separator. ex: /sample */\\n165:   cookie_path_len = strlen(cookie_path);\\n166:   if(1 == cookie_path_len) {\\n167:     /* cookie_path must be '/' */\\n168:     return TRUE;\\n169:   }\\n170: \\n171:   uri_path = strdup(request_uri);\\n172:   if(!uri_path)\\n173:     return FALSE;\\n174:   pos = strchr(uri_path, '?');\\n175:   if(pos)\\n176:     *pos = 0x0;\\n177: \\n178:   /* #-fragments are already cut off! */\\n179:   if(0 == strlen(uri_path) || uri_path[0] != '/') {\\n180:     strstore(&uri_path, \\\"/\\\", 1);\\n181:     if(!uri_path)\\n182:       return FALSE;\\n183:   }\\n184: \\n185:   /*\\n186:    * here, RFC6265 5.1.4 says\\n187:    *  4. domain));\\n240:       if(first)\\n241:         len -= (++first - domain);\\n242:     }\\n243:   }\\n244: \\n245:   if(outlen)\\n246:     *outlen = len;\\n247: \\n248:   return first? first: domain;\\n249: }\\n250: \\n251: /* Avoid C1001, an \\\"internal error\\\" with MSVC14 */\\n252: #if defined(_MSC_VER) && (_MSC_VER == 1900)\\n253: #pragma optimize(\\\"\\\", off)\\n254: #endif\\n255: \\n256: /*\\n257:  * A case-insensitive hash for the cookie domains.\\n258:  */\\n259: static size_t cookie_hash_domain(const char *domain, const size_t len)\\n260: {\\n261:   const char *end = domain + len;\\n262:   size_t h = 5381;\\n263: \\n264:   while(domain < end) {\\n265:     h += h << 5;\\n266:     h ^= Curl_raw_toupper(*domain++);\\n267:   }\\n268: \\n269:   return (h % COOKIE_HASH_SIZE);\\n270: }\\n271: \\n272: #if defined(_MSC_VER) && (_MSC_VER == 1900)\\n273: #pragma optimize(\\\"\\\", on)\\n274: #endif\\n275: \\n276: /*\\n277:  * Hash this domain.\\n278:  */\\n279: static size_t cookiehash(const char * const domain)\\n280: {\\n281:   const char *top;\\n282:   size_t len;\\n283: \\n284:   if(!domain || Curl_host_is_ipnum(domain))\\n285:     return 0;\\n286: \\n287:   top = get_top_domain(domain, &len);\\n288:   return cookie_hash_domain(top, len);\\n289: }\\n290: \\n291: /*\\n292:  * cookie path sanitize\\n293:  */\\n294: static char *sanitize_cookie_path(const char *cookie_path)\\n295: {\\n296:   size_t len;\\n297:   char *new_path = strdup(cookie_path);\\n298:   if(!new_path)\\n299:     return NULL;\\n300: \\n301:   /* some stupid site sends path attribute with '\\\"'. */\\n302:   len = strlen(new_path);\\n303:   if(new_path[0] == '\\\\\\\"') {\\n304:     memmove(new_path, new_path + 1, len);\\n305:     len--;\\n306:   }\\n307:   if(len && (new_path[len - The caller is responsible for checking\\n361:  * for OOM errors.\\n362:  */\\n363: static void strstore(char **str, const char *newstr, size_t len)\\n364: {\\n365:   DEBUGASSERT(newstr);\\n366:   DEBUGASSERT(str);\\n367:   free(*str);\\n368:   *str = Curl_memdup(newstr, len + 1);\\n369:   if(*str)\\n370:     (*str)[len] = 0;\\n371: }\\n372: \\n373: /*\\n374:  * remove_expired\\n375:  *\\n376:  * Remove expired cookies from the hash by inspecting the expires timestamp on\\n377:  * each cookie in the hash, freeing and deleting any where the timestamp is in\\n378:  * the past.  If the cookiejar has recorded the next timestamp at which one or\\n379:  * more cookies expire, then processing will exit early in case this timestamp\\n380:  * is in the future.\\n381:  */\\n382: static void remove_expired(struct CookieInfo *cookies)\\n383: {\\n384:   struct Cookie *co, *nx;\\n385:   curl_off_t now = (curl_off_t)time(NULL);\\n386:   unsigned int i;\\n387: \\n388:   /*\\n389:    * If the earliest expiration timestamp in the jar is in the future we can\\n390:    * skip scanning the whole jar and instead exit early as there won't be any\\n391:    * cookies to evict.  If we need to evict however, reset the next_expiration\\n392:    * counter in order to track the next one. In case the recorded first\\n393:    * expiration is the max offset, then perform the safe fallback of checking\\n394:    * all cookies.\\n395:    */\\n396:   if(now < cookies->next_expiration &&\\n397:       cookies->next_expiration != CURL_OFF_T_MAX)\\n398:     return;\\n399:   else\\n400:     cookies->next_expiration = CURL_OFF_T_MAX;\\n401: \\n402:   for(i = 0; i < COOKIE_HASH_SIZE; i++) {\\n403:     struct Cookie *pv = NULL;\\n404:     co = cookies->cookies[i];\\n405:     while(co) {\\n406:       nx = co->next;\\n407:       if(co->expires && co->expires < now) {\\n408:         if(!pv) {\\n409:           cookies->cookies[i] = co->next;\\n410:         }\\n411:         else {\\n412:           pv->next = co->next;\\n413:         }\\n414:         cookies->numcookies--;\\n415:         freecookie(co);\\n416:       }\\n417:       else {\\n418:         /*\\n419:          * If this cookie has an expiration timestamp earlier than what we've\\n420:          * seen so far then record it for the next round of expirations.\\n421:          */\\n422:         if(co->expires && co->expires < cookies->next_expiration)\\n423:           cookies->next_expiration = co->expires;\\n424:         pv = co;\\n425:       }\\n426:       co = nx;\\n427:     }\\n428:   }\\n429: }\\n430: \\n431: /* Make sure domain contains a dot or is localhost. */\\n432: static bool bad_domain(const char *domain, size_t len)\\n433: {\\n434:   if((len == 9) && strncasecompare(domain, \\\"localhost\\\", 9))\\n435:     return FALSE;\\n436:   else {\\n437:     /* there must be a dot present, but that dot must not be a trailing dot */\\n438:     char *dot = memchr(domain, '.', len);\\n439:     if(dot) {\\n440:       size_t i = dot - domain;\\n441:       if((len - i) > 1)\\n442:         /* the dot is not the last byte */\\n443:         return FALSE;\\n444:     }\\n445:   }\\n446:   return TRUE;\\n447: }\\n448: \\n449: /*\\n450:   RFC 6265 section 4.1.1 says a server should accept this range:\\n451: \\n452:   cookie-octet    = %x21 / %x23-2B / %x2D-3A / %x3C-5B / %x5D-7E\\n453: \\n454:   But Firefox and Chrome as of June 2022 accept space, comma and double-quotes\\n455:   fine. Be aware that\\n476:  * sometimes we get an IP-only host name, and that might also be a numerical\\n477:  * IPv6 address.\\n478:  *\\n479:  * Returns NULL on out of memory or invalid cookie. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Sc9pBjsZbp6w9ZbdjxiHX5","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"I found an issue! Looking at lines 2166-2177:\n\n```c\n#ifdef ENABLE_IPV6\n  if(conn->bits.ipv6_ip &&\n     Curl_inet_pton(AF_INET6, hostname, &addr)) {\n    target = GEN_IPADD;\n    addrlen = sizeof(struct in6_addr);\n  }\n  else\n#endif\n    if(Curl_inet_pton(AF_INET, hostname, &addr)) {\n      target = GEN_IPADD;\n      addrlen = sizeof(struct in_addr);\n    }\n```\n\nThe problem is:\n1. On line 2146, `addrlen` is initialized to 0 \n2. If neither the IPv6 check nor the IPv4 check succeed (e.g., `conn->bits.ipv6_ip` is false or Curl_inet_pton fails), then `addrlen` remains 0\n3. When comparing in the GEN_IPADD case at line 2237: `if((altlen == addrlen) && !memcmp(altptr, &addr, altlen))`\n4. If `addrlen == 0`, then `altlen` must also be 0 for the comparison to proceed\n5. But more importantly, if Curl_inet_pton failed, `addr` was never properly initialized, yet it could still be compared. This is uninitialized memory usage.\n\nActually, let me reconsider. The `addr` struct is declared on the stack, so if it's not initialized, it contains garbage. If the check `if(altlen == addrlen)` succeeds and addrlen was never set (so it's 0), then altlen must also be 0, which means this path is skipped. So that's safe.\n\nBut wait, there's another issue. What if `Curl_inet_pton` is called but `ENABLE_IPV6` is not defined? The else branch will always be executed. \n\nBut if ENABLE_IPV6 is defined and `conn->bits.ipv6_ip` is true, Curl_inet_pton(AF_INET6, ...) is called first. If that fails, we fall through to the else block which attempts the IPv4 check. The structure is: if IPv6 succeeds, we're done; otherwise (else), try IPv4. So if IPv6 parsing fails, the code does attempt IPv4 as a fallback.\n\nNow I'm wondering what the actual problem is. When both checks fail and addrlen remains 0, IP address validation from the certificate can't proceed properly. Looking more closely at line 2210, there's an issue with how the certificate data is being extracted.\n\nThe union member `check->d.ia5` is accessed without verifying that `check->d` is actually initialized for this particular type. Depending on the GENERAL_NAME type, the union could contain different data, potentially causing out-of-bounds memory reads. I should examine the transfer.c file to see if there are similar issues If `global_passwd` is NULL, this will cause a segfault. There's no NULL check before dereferencing it.\n\nAlso, another issue: the condition at line 964 checks `if(num > klen)`.
